  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13696788409256665642">Mara Dyer knows she isn't crazy. She knows that she can kill with her mind, and that Noah can heal with his. Mara also knows that somehow, Jude is not a hallucination. He is alive. Unfortunately, convincing her family and doctors that she's not unstable and doesn't need to be hospitalised isn't easy. The only person who actually believes her is Noah. But being with Noah is</span>
  <span id="freeText13696788409256665642" style="display:none">Mara Dyer knows she isn't crazy. She knows that she can kill with her mind, and that Noah can heal with his. Mara also knows that somehow, Jude is not a hallucination. He is alive. Unfortunately, convincing her family and doctors that she's not unstable and doesn't need to be hospitalised isn't easy. The only person who actually believes her is Noah. But being with Noah is dangerous and Mara is in constant fear that she might hurt him. She needs to learn how to control her power, and fast! Together, Mara and Noah must try and figure out exactly how Jude survived when the asylum collapsed, and how he knows so much about her strange ability...before anyone else ends up dead!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13696788409256665642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_17334499').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_17334499').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_17334499').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {

<div id="review_240883938" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240883938" />
    <a title="Vy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4612408-vy"><img alt="Vy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517020329p2/4612408.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/240883938?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vy" href="/user/show/4612408-vy">Vy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442421790" href="/book/show/12950372-the-evolution-of-mara-dyer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4612408-vy?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4612408-vy?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4612408-vy?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4612408-vy?shelf=2012-sophomore">2012-sophomore</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240883938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10416075818612419424">ALL THE STARS RIGHT HERE.<br/>Can we all just slow clap for this?<br/><p>
  <img height='161' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380363983ra/715508.gif' width='285' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</p><br/>AND THIS BOOK. NO WORDS RIGHT NOW. I just..<br/><p>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/657013.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</p><br/>My thoughts have yet to make sense. So for now, all you have to know is that Evolution is a fantastic book that will most likely be the source of my nightmares and paranoia for the next few days.<br/><br/>GO PRE-ORDER NOW! I just ordered mine :)<br/><br/>***********updated FULL review***********<br/><br/>I wasn't sure how it could be possible, but The Evolution of Mara Dyer was even more intese and twisted than The </span>
  <span id="freeText10416075818612419424" style="display:none">ALL THE STARS RIGHT HERE.<br>Can we all just slow clap for this?<br><p>
  <img height="161" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380363983ra/715508.gif" width="285" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br>AND THIS BOOK. NO WORDS RIGHT NOW. I just..<br><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/657013.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br>My thoughts have yet to make sense. So for now, all you have to know is that Evolution is a fantastic book that will most likely be the source of my nightmares and paranoia for the next few days.<br><br>GO PRE-ORDER NOW! I just ordered mine :)<br><br>***********updated FULL review***********<br><br>I wasn't sure how it could be possible, but The Evolution of Mara Dyer was even more intese and twisted than The Unbecoming.<br><br><b>Before reading:</b> Huh, my book is signed with, "Who will you believe?" Interesting. Well I guess I'll go with Michelle Hodkin. <br><br><b>After reading:</b> NO ONE. I BELIEVE NO ONE. EXCEPT NOAH SHAW. I WILL BELIEVE EVERYTHING HE SAYS.<br><br>The Evolution goes into Mara's family history as well as Noah's. I would think that I would be able to make some theories from that, but nope. Fret not people, even though new information was tossed in, there were a lot of questions answered from The Unbecoming. I never looked at anything the same through out this book. One moment I would feel like I was finally putting the story together, but then I would turn the page and all of my theories would get burned.<br><br>There were so many "what just happened moments". At first I would try to make some sense out of it, but after a while I just rolled with it. Kind of. I started categorizing my reactions to those moments into the "my life after finishing" list, and this was what I got.<br><br><b>My Life After Finishing The Evolution of Mara Dyer:</b><br>Day 1: Maybe I'll just leave my lamp on tonight.<br>Day 2: I'll just turn ALL the lights on in my house.<br>Day 3: Maybe I should just not clear the fog from my mirror after taking a shower.<br>Day 4: SUPER PARANOID. NOBODY TOUCH ME. <br>Day 5: Has brother stand next to me while I brush my teeth.<br><br>One of the many things I loved about this book was Mara Dyer and Noah Shaw. They just work. It is how it is. They will forever be one of my favorite couples.<br><br>I loved every moment of The Evolution of Mara Dyer. Even though Mara Dyer is the reason I can't look into the mirror after I take a shower, I will read anything by Michelle Hodkin.</span>

<div id="review_1137395963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1137395963" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1137395963?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1137395963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6734190548297204190"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Tell me what you see. Because I don't know what's real and what isn't or what's new or different and I can't trust myself, but I trust you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>I am <b>confused</b>. And <s>scared</s> <b>terrified</b>. I am <b>angry</b>. I am <b>freaked out</b>. I am unconditionally and irrevocably <b>in love</b> with this series. And <b>it hurts</b>.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380764962ra/3121205.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You will love him to ruins.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>When a book starts with this line, you know that things are going to get ugly. In <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13643567.The_Evolution_of_Mara_Dyer__Mara_Dyer___2_' title='The Evolution of Mara Dyer (Mara Dyer, #2) by Michelle Hodkin' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Evolution of Mara Dyer</a> Mara's family is seriously concerned about her mental </span>
  <span id="freeText6734190548297204190" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Tell me what you see. Because I don't know what's real and what isn't or what's new or different and I can't trust myself, but I trust you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I am <b>confused</b>. And <s>scared</s> <b>terrified</b>. I am <b>angry</b>. I am <b>freaked out</b>. I am unconditionally and irrevocably <b>in love</b> with this series. And <b>it hurts</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380764962ra/3121205.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You will love him to ruins.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>When a book starts with this line, you know that things are going to get ugly. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13643567.The_Evolution_of_Mara_Dyer__Mara_Dyer___2_" title="The Evolution of Mara Dyer (Mara Dyer, #2) by Michelle Hodkin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Evolution of Mara Dyer</a> Mara's family is seriously concerned about her mental state and decides that severe treatment is the only way to get their daughter back. The thing is, Mara is not crazy but pretends to acknowledge that she is crazy in order to stay out of mental institutions, but she's afraid that she will lose her sanity if she doesn't get answers. Answers about her powers, the ghost from her past that seems to h(a)unt, her grandmother, some identical pendants and a creepy doll. The only person who really knows what's happening to her is Noah, but Noah has problems of his own and secrets he can't share. And their love alone is not enough.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I was falling apart, and all my pieces were scattering to the wind.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Helplessness, despair, anger, frustration</b>,y ou are trapped in a <b>whirlwind of emotions</b> that make you grasp for breath, something that never comes. You want to claw your brain to erase the throbbing, to press your nails in your hands until they bleed, to untie that knot in your stomach. That's what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13643567.The_Evolution_of_Mara_Dyer__Mara_Dyer___2_" title="The Evolution of Mara Dyer (Mara Dyer, #2) by Michelle Hodkin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Evolution of Mara Dyer</a> did to me. It was <b>creepy</b>, so creepy that I couldn't sleep without the lights on, that the concept of the monsters that lurk in the dark seemed somehow real. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4126827.Michelle_Hodkin" title="Michelle Hodkin" rel="nofollow noopener">Michelle Hodkin</a> found her way into my brain and into my heart, and I am scared of what she'll do with that power. And that ending left me in the verge of hysteria.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385601950ra/7183228.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“This was the boy I loved. A little bit messy. A little bit ruined. A beautiful disaster. Just like me.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Noah Elliot Simon Shaw, you are one of the loves of my life.</b> This arrogant, dedicated and broken boy was the only source of light in Mara's life, his love the only stable thing in a world that was falling apart. He and Mara had their issues, but together they were strong, they made me strong, strong enough to withstand the forceful attack against my sanity this book launched.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I can't slay the dragon because I can't find him, so for now I stay close.<br>It's not enough.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>A beautifully disturbing book</b>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13643567.The_Evolution_of_Mara_Dyer__Mara_Dyer___2_" title="The Evolution of Mara Dyer (Mara Dyer, #2) by Michelle Hodkin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Evolution of Mara Dyer</a> led to shocking events and revelations that made me want to read the final book even more desperately than before. I pray Michelle will be merciful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6734190548297204190" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5109253-anna?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5109253-anna?shelf=my-bookshelf">my-bookshelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227082400" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15104016077592475665">I should probably write a real review for this. Maybe I will, when my head isn't reeling.<br/><br/>The Evolution is everything that The Unbecoming was and more. Romantic, perfectly paced, repeatedly punching you in the gut... I actually had to take a bunch of breaks and purge to someone during the last 100 pages because everything was becoming so intense and scary and twisted. It's 10 times worse than The Unbecoming, and it's awesome.<br/><br/>It also raised my standards for gore and fear. If I had to pick two word</span>
  <span id="freeText15104016077592475665" style="display:none">I should probably write a real review for this. Maybe I will, when my head isn't reeling.<br /><br />The Evolution is everything that The Unbecoming was and more. Romantic, perfectly paced, repeatedly punching you in the gut... I actually had to take a bunch of breaks and purge to someone during the last 100 pages because everything was becoming so intense and scary and twisted. It's 10 times worse than The Unbecoming, and it's awesome.<br /><br />It also raised my standards for gore and fear. If I had to pick two words to describe this book, I'd say: Hot. And freaky.<br /><br />Really, I would recommend this series to anyone who likes the intensity. It's not for the easily scared or the faint of heart. The webs of the plot just keep getting deeper and tying together in new ways, and the romance keeps evolving. I always loved the way Hodkin creates scenes that are so, so sexy, without ever being too innocent and YA-like, and without ever veering into dirty, now-I-have-to-go-shower territory. Mara and Noah are as spirited as ever, and I loved Mara's family, as usual (the mother is exempt.)<br /><br />A word of warning: The cliffhanger is even worse than The Unbecoming. I'm almost sorry I read this early. Almost. But what did I expect, when The Evolution was so much more intense, so much scarier, so much more sick and beautiful and gut-wrenching?<br /><br /><br />*Thanks to Simon and Schuster for the ARC.</span>

<div id="review_1711218567" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1711218567" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1711218567?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      Everyone, duh! 
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=lol">lol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=psycho">psycho</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1711218567" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2913241455428397133"><br/>I just finished the book and I’m totally freaking out and silently screaming obscene phrases at the air because man, that twist, that ending (or the lack of it), as picked up from the book, is batshit crazy. I’m not sure if I should applaud it or curse it. I’m not sure whether to be impressed or upset by the revelations and I guess that’s when you can say a book is really good- when it totally messes up with your head. Up to now, my heartbeat hasn’t returned to normal. It hasn’t since I started </span>
  <span id="freeText2913241455428397133" style="display:none"><br>I just finished the book and I’m totally freaking out and silently screaming obscene phrases at the air because man, that twist, that ending (or the lack of it), as picked up from the book, is batshit crazy. I’m not sure if I should applaud it or curse it. I’m not sure whether to be impressed or upset by the revelations and I guess that’s when you can say a book is really good- when it totally messes up with your head. Up to now, my heartbeat hasn’t returned to normal. It hasn’t since I started reading the book, I mean devouring it (took me only two afternoons to finish it).<br><br>In the first book, Mara Dyer is the hero/anti-hero who blames herself for the death of her best friend. She starts seeing, hearing and feeling weird things which her family and doctors dismiss as simply symptoms of PTSD. In the second book, her symptoms seem to aggravate and require extreme psychological/medical intervention. But the huge question is, is she really just seeing things or could they be products of a paranormal phenomenon or is it entirely something else? Tag along with Noah (my love) and Mara as they uncover these mysteries about themselves and more.<br><br>Still told in the extremely unreliable voice of Mara, the story is an equally riveting read as its predecessor laced with mystery, humor, sarcasm, romance and most of all, absolute creepiness (which explains why my heart won’t stay in its rightful place the entire time I was reading.) <br><br>I won’t say more because I'm going to dive into the third book because I need to know what happens and I really have to prove my existing theories true. I’m seriously hoping I’m right because if not, the third book shall incur my wrath! <br><br>Third book, I’m definitely ready!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469672193ra/19843173.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="2913241455428397133" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780857073655" href="/book/show/16108212-the-evolution-of-mara-dyer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=young-adult-books">young-adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=supernatural-stuff">supernatural-stuff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer771714185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7277925931911564624"><i>Pre-review:</i><br/><br/>I'm at page. 255 and I want to list out a few things I wish Michelle Hodkin would write in the remaining part of <i>The Evolution of Mara Dyer</i>:<br/><br/><b>(1) Mara is in fact crazy.<br/><br/>(2) Jude, Mara's ex-boyfriend and would-be-rapist, is in fact dead.<br/><br/>(3)Whenever Mara thinks she's seeing Jude, it's only her seeing her imaginary stalker.<br/><br/>(4) Every single spooky event that has taken place in the book is either Mara's own handiwork or they taken place only in her head.<br/><br/>(5) Mara goes all psycho-bitch and kill</b></span>
  <span id="freeText7277925931911564624" style="display:none"><i>Pre-review:</i><br /><br />I'm at page. 255 and I want to list out a few things I wish Michelle Hodkin would write in the remaining part of <i>The Evolution of Mara Dyer</i>:<br /><br /><b>(1) Mara is in fact crazy.<br /><br />(2) Jude, Mara's ex-boyfriend and would-be-rapist, is in fact dead.<br /><br />(3)Whenever Mara thinks she's seeing Jude, it's only her seeing her imaginary stalker.<br /><br />(4) Every single spooky event that has taken place in the book is either Mara's own handiwork or they taken place only in her head.<br /><br />(5) Mara goes all psycho-bitch and kills Noah, her boyfriend.<br /><br />(6) Mara goes all psycho-bitch and kills her family members.</b><br /><br />If any of these things really take place, it would definitely make my day!<br /><br />NOTE: I did a buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8365976-alice-kat-error-nebula" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice</a> when reading this book.<br /><br /><b>Rating: it's a 'I can't give a flying fuck to a book which keeps refusing to make sense' negative stars.</b><br /><br />Since there's no such thing as negative stars in the GR rating system, I had to make do with one star.<br /><br />Supposedly I should feel sorry for Mara Dyer, because our Super Special Lovely Snowflake Heroine is being wrongly accused of being insane. But for the life in me, how can I feel sorry for her when she keeps acting like a psycho-bitch and talking down at almost every single mental patient in the story?<br /><br />As to Mara's love interest Noah...well he is in fact <i>better</i> in this second book, but I still hate his cocky guts and the way he seems to think he can buy everything and everyone with his big wallet. I know, Noah is from a super rich family and he clearly has money to burn, but still.<br /><br />Michelle Hodkin's writing is in fact <i>slightly</i> better than the first book as well; sadly the writing still isn't good enough to cover up for the massive, larger-than-life flaws which plagued the entire book, namely:<br /><br /><b>(1.) The cheesy, going-nowhere romance between Noah and Mara: </b>Although I'm glad that there's no love triangle in the book, but I still can't see what's so deep and meaningful about two teenagers going on about "Oh you're so beautiful, I want to kiss you, but NO! I can't kiss you because it'll kill you! I want to sex you up behind your parents' back but NO! We can't do it! It's not right!"<br /><br />Give me a break.<br /><br /><b>(2.) The mind-numbing boredom:</b> There's no revelation, no plot twists, no development, until the very end.<br /><br /><b>(3.)The 'so-bad-it's-bad' attempts at create tension and suspense:</b> I felt like I was watching a poorly made horror movie whenever Miss Hodkin tries to scare her readers with her 'spooky scenes'.<br /><br /><b>(4.)Author being greedy and doesn't know where to stop:</b> This time, we have Jude haunting Mara, we have Mara trying to pretend she's normal, we have the drama about the fortuneteller's foretelling Noah's death, we have this mysterious, never-explained Abel Lukumi character hopping in and out at random, we have Noah's family being somehow connected to Mara's grandmother and we also have Mara's late grandmother and the spooky events took place years ago back in India <i>and</i> Mara having random flashbacks about it? Last but not least, we also have <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ some evil doctors running shady experiments on Mara, Noah and the rest of the teenage patients in the program? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> That's just too fucking much.<br /><br /><b>(5.)Mara's constantly making rude remarks on mental illness and mental patients</b>: What can I say...whenever I started to think the writing is getting good, Mara the Main Character just has to start badmouthing mentally ill people <i>AGAIN</i>. Oh yes, she had already started it in book 1, but now in the book 2, she's at it again. For example, she calls a fellow teenage patient in the program <b>'a psycho'</b> before addressing said patient as <b>'batshit crazy'</b> in front of the whole group. <br /><br />Rude, isn't it? It sounds to me like Mara really thinks she's too innocent and special to suffer mental illness, she also whines nonstop about other people labeling her as crazy the whole time! But our heroine still thinks it's within her right to judge and label someone else as 'crazy' and 'psycho'.<br /><br />Double standards, how lovely. <br /><br />And then our lovely heroine also comes up with the following line:<br /><br /><i>But with something else (schizophrenia)---this was it for me. A lifetime of psych ward and medication. No college. No life.(page. 33)</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>NO LIFE?</i>
</b><br /><br />Okay, let's be frank here. No one wants to suffer schizophrenia, no one wants to be locked in a psych ward; but does it mean people who suffer schizophrenia <b>'have no life?'</b> Mara, when will you stop making mental illness sounds like the most scary, disgusting thing on earth? That's fucking disrespectful, it's fucking <i>discrimination</i>; if you asked me.<br /><br />By the end of the story, I can't believe <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[after it's revealed that Jude's special power is to drain the life-force of other creatures around him whenever he is injured, in the final showdown between him and Mara, there already are two teenagers being drained by Jude, but for the whole time Mara DID NOTHING to save those two barely breathing teens; instead Mara just keeps beating Jude whilst the two teenagers are lying nearby, with their life force being sucked dry? WTF? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I am done! I can deal with the MC being a psycho bitch, but I CAN'T DEAL WITH THE MC BEING A COLD HEARTENED BITCH WHO DOESN'T CARE ABOUT TWO OTHER TEENS DYING AT HER FEET! <br /><br />After this point, I just don't care about this book anymore.<br /><br />Review for book 1: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/521482021?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7277925931911564624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1465769662" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1465769662" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1465769662?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1465769662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10306419847392607639">I think my brain melted. Like, actually, that is my brain, on the floor, in a puddle of <i>what even</i>. JUST IN CASE YOU WERE CURIOUS AS TO MY REACTION TO THIS BOOK. Okay...deeeep breaths. <b>I did love it, but I had several "WHAT EVEN THE HECK" moments that confused me too much.</b> <br/><br/><b>Also this book is too huge. </b>Way too huge. It dribbles on <i>so much</i> in the middle it was actually irritating??? Which is a shame because book 1 was perfection. I have yet to meet a YA book that's over 500 words which I feel <i>needed</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10306419847392607639" style="display:none">I think my brain melted. Like, actually, that is my brain, on the floor, in a puddle of <i>what even</i>. JUST IN CASE YOU WERE CURIOUS AS TO MY REACTION TO THIS BOOK. Okay...deeeep breaths. <b>I did love it, but I had several "WHAT EVEN THE HECK" moments that confused me too much.</b> <br /><br /><b>Also this book is too huge. </b>Way too huge. It dribbles on <i>so much</i> in the middle it was actually irritating??? Which is a shame because book 1 was perfection. I have yet to meet a YA book that's over 500 words which I feel <i>needed</i> all those words. <br /><br />BUT ANYWAY. <b>A quick list of my complaints </b>and then onto my fangirling.<br />• Mara's parents let Noah stay over...a lot. And they, believe shenanigans won't go down?? BAH AHAHA. What idiot parents. -_-<br />• Also while I ship Noah and Mara like nothing else (because they are cute and needful)...their romance almost felt <i>too</i> old? Like I felt they were in their 20s, not 17 at times? It's not graphically or sexual or anything, don't get me wrong -- but it <b>doesn't feel like a TEEN romance.</b><br />• Jamie's potential is STILL wasted, dangit.<br />• There is a huge "AFJDKSLAFDJ WUT WUT NO NO" moment at the end, but because the book is like 95% "is this real or not real"...I didn't get thumped by the plot twist. I don't know if it's real? So I'm not even concerned. So either a) the book is to blame, or b) I'm a cold-hearted monster. Hmm. Let's go with a)?<br />• It was too freaking long. TOO FREAKING LONG, I SAY.<br /><br /><br />....Okay, but you know what?! <b>I still absolutely totally astronomically loved it.</b> There's something about the writing??! It's so dreamy and dark and nightmarish. And the writing weaves in the supernatural with the contemporary SO PERFECTLY.<br /><br /><b>Plus I'm a big fan of unreliable narrators.</b> If you think Mara was unhinged in book 1....hahahaha, oh darling. SHE GETS WORSE. She loses memory. Loses time. Sleep walks. Is noted giving deranged laughs after bad stuff goes down. And she's falling apart <i>and she knows it.</i> It was like a spiral downwards and I couldn't look away. Also it was SO SO SAD because she's experiencing all this <i>evil stuff</i> and no one believes her and is diagnosing her a schizophrenic. <br /><br />...which, come to think on it, makes me wonder about my stance on this. Like is this what it's LIKE to develop schizophrenia? Is the book saying schizophrenics are really just seeing another world and aren't crazy? I'm...I'm unsure how to feel about the niggly details, tbh. <b>It didn't spoil the story for me, personally, but I wonder if the book would be offensive to someone actually suffering with schizophrenia or knowing someone who is?</b> Things to ponder...<br /><br />OKAY and even though the ending plot twist didn't stab me...<b>I STILL AM FREAKING UNPLEASED OKAY?!??!?! </b> Take it back.<i> Take it back right now and make things okay.</i> Omgggggg. I need book 3 <i>immediately</i> and my library doesn't have it so I'm going to have to sit here in PAIN. INDEFINITE PAIN. <br /><br />There were plenty of hospitals, asylums, creepy dolls, and witty banter (thank goodness for the banter). I confess to being partially in love with the insufferably smart and gorgeous Noah (!!) and just rooting for Mara to figure out the mystery behind all of this (!!) and I <i>love</i> the emphasis on family and how much <i>horror-y</i> (that is a word!) this book is. <b>I LOVE IT AND I WANT MORE.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10306419847392607639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer17148231921961564694"> <u>Just one word</u>: <b>AMAZING</b> <br/><br/>I can not stop thinking about what just happened......<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444044534ra/16445934.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><u>This book as the first has left me wondering many things and my head is a mess! unexpected information ... WOW !!</u><br/><br/><b>I am pleasantly surprised honestly had my doubts about whether this book could overcome the first and really did with honors!</b><br/><br/><br/><i>Michelle God! , I wish to have only a quarter of the talent that this woman possesses. It has become one of my favorite writers with only two books I have read, I would read anything t</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17148231921961564694" style="display:none"> <u>Just one word</u>: <b>AMAZING</b> <br><br>I can not stop thinking about what just happened......<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444044534ra/16445934.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>This book as the first has left me wondering many things and my head is a mess! unexpected information ... WOW !!</u><br><br><b>I am pleasantly surprised honestly had my doubts about whether this book could overcome the first and really did with honors!</b><br><br><br><i>Michelle God! , I wish to have only a quarter of the talent that this woman possesses. It has become one of my favorite writers with only two books I have read, I would read anything that Michelle wrote.</i><br><br><b>The Evolution of Mara Dyer has had ALL!! so many emotions fear, joy, love and suspense that characterized certainly this series have killed me! (In a good clear sense)</b><br><br>I'm so in love with the main characters I really suffer a lot for them especially <b>Mara </b>she has become such a strong woman! I'm so proud of her!.<br><br>Every part of his story from his search for truth, what is real and what is not, all that mystery, even as it struggles to appear normal trying to ignore what happens is so brave, it really is a book that plays with your mind and that makes it very difficult to leave<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411831319i/11284407._SX540_.jpg" width="500" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Noah</b> is still one of my greatest literary love of all time !!!!!!<br>And it remains a character no waste ;)<br><br><blockquote>“If I were to live a thousand years, I would belong to you for all of them. If we were to live a thousand lives, I would want to make you mine in each one.” <br>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Jude, Jude, Jude if it is a character worthy of hate...</b><br>It is a dark and cruel character who does not mind doing absolutely nothing to get their goal and this is not good for Mara<br><br> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[AND ALSO HAVE POWERS! so convenient! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br> <b>And that end! is that this book as the first have these incredible end just kill your head trying to understand but we can not until the next book ....</b><br><br><blockquote>“You can't hurt me the way you think you can. But even if you could? I would rather die with the taste of you on my tongue than live and never touch you again. I'm in love with you, Mara. I love you. No matter what you do.” </blockquote><br><br> <b>REVELATIONS EVERYWHERE!!</b><br><br> <u>Oh my God! I am loving this series dying to continue it</u>..<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_269519763" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/269519763" />
    <a title="Joie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6224284-joie"><img alt="Joie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453104735p2/6224284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/269519763?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joie" href="/user/show/6224284-joie">Joie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442421790" href="/book/show/12950372-the-evolution-of-mara-dyer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6224284-joie?shelf=swoon-worthy-guy">swoon-worthy-guy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6224284-joie?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6224284-joie?shelf=need-to-buy">need-to-buy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6224284-joie?shelf=creepy">creepy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6224284-joie?shelf=amazeballs">amazeballs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer269519763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10455889794433813106">The unfortunate byproduct of being a high school senior is that I don't have much time to read. Not as much as I used to, anyway. Before, I was able to finish a book in less than a week, and now, quite frankly, I'm lucky if I make it through half of the book in that time.<br/><br/>This book took me three days to finish.<br/><br/>Three days.<br/><br/>GUYS. <i>THREE DAYS.</i><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380368566ra/721156.gif' width='350' height='240' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Insanity. I don't even remember the last time I finished a book so quickly.<br/><br/>So here's how it all went down....<br/><br/><b>Me before reading:</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380368566ra/721157.gif' width='330' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Beyond excited. In fact, I may (or</span>
  <span id="freeText10455889794433813106" style="display:none">The unfortunate byproduct of being a high school senior is that I don't have much time to read. Not as much as I used to, anyway. Before, I was able to finish a book in less than a week, and now, quite frankly, I'm lucky if I make it through half of the book in that time.<br><br>This book took me three days to finish.<br><br>Three days.<br><br>GUYS. <i>THREE DAYS.</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380368566ra/721156.gif" width="350" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Insanity. I don't even remember the last time I finished a book so quickly.<br><br>So here's how it all went down....<br><br><b>Me before reading:</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380368566ra/721157.gif" width="330" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Beyond excited. In fact, I may (or may not have) done a happy dance when I finally had the book in my hands. And this happy dance may or may not have been incredibly embarrassing and performed in public...<br><br><b>Me while reading:</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380368566ra/721158.gif" width="340" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book was an addiction. It's fast-paced and full of creepiness, revelations, and sexy times with Noah, and if you think you can just stop after one chapter, you are lying to yourself.<br><br>The stakes, suspense, and mystery are all elevated in Evolution. More than ever, you see Mara's sanity being put in question, to the point where she doesn't even know whether or not she's experiencing reality or a delusion. Reading this story was akin to playing a mind game Half the time I was trying to figure out who to believe, what the truth really was, and the other half, I was questioning everything I thought.<br><br>Unlike many YA books, Evolution really included Mara's family into what was going on. Her parents aren't absentees or idle spectators. They see their daughter in trouble and they act. And don't even get me started on the sibling relationship in the Dyer family because I won't be able to stop gushing! Mara's relationship with her brothers, Daniel especially, was just incredibly realistic and SO sweet. It definitely made me wish I had an older brother like Daniel.<br><br>My favorite part of this book, though, was seeing more of Mara and Noah's relationship. At the beginning of the series, it seemed like the only thing really tying the two of them together was their inexplicable abilities. In this book, however, it becomes so much more apparent that these two are perfect for each other! I think it's safe to say that they are both quite screwed up as a result of their respective powers, but when they're together, they make each other better (which sounds cheesy, I know, but there's really no way to describe it!) They keep each other grounded when everything around them is questionable.<br><br>I especially enjoyed seeing more of Noah's character. He wasn't exactly a flat character in Unbecoming, but I definitely didn't get to know him as much as I wanted to. Evolution did a great job of showing me more of Noah Elliot Simon Shaw and I <i>loved</i> it.<br><br>Eep.<br><br>Help.<br><br>I'm swooning.<br><br><b>Me after reading:</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380368566ra/721159.gif" width="330" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380368566ra/721160.gif" width="350" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In Unbecoming, I was full of questions, wondering just what the heck Mara was and how it was possible that she could do the things she did. In Evolution, it feels like Michelle Hodkin is finally letting you in on the big secret.... but it's all a big. Fat. Lie!!! It's like she's dangling this delicious-looking carrot of truth in front of you, making you read page after page after page, but in the end, all you are left with is a blown mind and more questions. Oh, and frustration. Heaps of that. Well played Ms. Hodkin, well played. <br><br><b>Rating: 5 stars</b><br><br>Dear Ms. Hodkin,<br><br>Book three....<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/438061.gif" width="320" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Pretty please?</span>
  <a data-text-id="10455889794433813106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/3471319-jen">Jen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442421790" href="/book/show/12950372-the-evolution-of-mara-dyer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3471319-jen?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227823004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14416745741472861650">Originally posted here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.makeshiftbookmark.com/2012/07/my-thoughts-evolution-of-mara-dyer-by.html'>http://www.makeshiftbookmark.com/2012...</a><br/><br/>OH.<br/>MY.<br/>EVER.<br/>LOVING. <br/>HELL.<br/><br/>The Evolution of Mara Dyer has just infiltrated and plundered my brain and I can't sleep until I tell you about it.<br/><br/>You know that feeling that you hope and wish for every time you read a book but, more often than not, are underwhelmed? That notion where, "hey, what good is life anyway if I'm not reading this very book in this very moment?" That moment when you build up this elaborate hypothesis in your brain a</span>
  <span id="freeText14416745741472861650" style="display:none">Originally posted here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.makeshiftbookmark.com/2012/07/my-thoughts-evolution-of-mara-dyer-by.html">http://www.makeshiftbookmark.com/2012...</a><br /><br />OH.<br />MY.<br />EVER.<br />LOVING. <br />HELL.<br /><br />The Evolution of Mara Dyer has just infiltrated and plundered my brain and I can't sleep until I tell you about it.<br /><br />You know that feeling that you hope and wish for every time you read a book but, more often than not, are underwhelmed? That notion where, "hey, what good is life anyway if I'm not reading this very book in this very moment?" That moment when you build up this elaborate hypothesis in your brain and you're all, "I KNOW how this should end, why doesn't the author just let me take the reins from here on out, mmkay thanks," but then you're introduced to a conclusion (or cliffhanger, such is the case) that rattles every molecule of your being to the point where you're going to lose your shiz for the next 365+ days until you get that soul-slaying conclusion to one of those most enthralling, possessing series that you've ever read in your 27 years of life?<br /><br />Yeah, this book has those things.<br /><br />If you were left scrambled after The Unbecoming of Mara Dyer, I have good news for you. You get some answers. (And OH MY GOD, Noah. He loves her so, so much. It's insane.)<br /><br />But then there's an ass ton of new information that will leave you sitting there with a pen and paper, eyes darting to and fro, trying to divy up your attentions between devouring this book and fiercely mapping out flow charts to try and make sense of what mastermind Michelle Hodkin is illustrating before your eyes.<br /><br />I did get a little nervous at one point that it was taking a spin towards WTF-territory. But then I learned to bask in the WTFery. I trust where this is going. I always trust the unreliable narrators. It'll all come together, through hell or high water.<br /><br />I'm sleep-deprived but shameless in my love and devotion to this series and this author. If the world ends before I read The Retribution of Mara Dyer, I will be seriously pissed. Dead, but pissed. I will have no remorse for the amount of poltergeisting I will do.<br /><br />Preorder. Like now. I will be buying two. (I need one where I can highlight and circle and star and draw gnarly sketches of Noah and Mara kissing, cuddling, getting married in the margins around all my favorite lines. Photographic evidence to come.)</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/930026981?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)" href="/user/show/21937982-hailey-hailey-in-bookland">Hailey (Hailey in Bookland)</a>

        rated it

I love trying to figure out what's going on. Also really love all the characters but sometimes I just got so frustrated wanting people to believe Mara!!! </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_436888226" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/436888226" />
    <a title="destini mia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13742215-destini-mia"><img alt="destini mia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499903277p2/13742215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/436888226?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destini mia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destini mia" href="/user/show/13742215-destini-mia">destini mia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442421790" href="/book/show/12950372-the-evolution-of-mara-dyer">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer436888226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7568651930158196512"><br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote> “I’m afraid– I’m afraid I’m losing control.” I’m afraid I’m losing myself. The idea was a splinter in my mind. Always there, always stinging, even when I wasn’t conscious of it. Even when I wasn’t thinking about it. </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/><u>What did I just read?</u> My emotions are all over the place. Just when I thought I was getting answers, Michelle Hodkin slams me over the head with some grade A mindf*ckery. But who the hell am I fooling? I loved every second of it. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>*<u>All spoilers tagged </u> *</b>
</i><br/><i>
  <blockquote>Mara Dyer o</blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText7568651930158196512" style="display:none"><br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote> “I’m afraid– I’m afraid I’m losing control.” I’m afraid I’m losing myself. The idea was a splinter in my mind. Always there, always stinging, even when I wasn’t conscious of it. Even when I wasn’t thinking about it. </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br /><u>What did I just read?</u> My emotions are all over the place. Just when I thought I was getting answers, Michelle Hodkin slams me over the head with some grade A mindf*ckery. But who the hell am I fooling? I loved every second of it. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>*<u>All spoilers tagged </u> *</b>
</i><br /><i>
  <blockquote>Mara Dyer once believed she could run from her past.<br /><b>She can’t.</b><br /><br />She used to think her problems were all in her head.<br /><b>They aren’t.</b><br /><br />She couldn’t imagine that after everything she’s been through, the boy she loves would still be keeping secrets.<br /><b>She’s wrong.</b><br /><br />In this gripping sequel to The Unbecoming of Mara Dyer, the truth evolves and choices prove deadly. What will become of Mara Dyer next?</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Things pick up practically where we left of in The Unbecoming of Mara Dyer. It's a couple days after <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[her father was shot and Jude made an appearance at the police station. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Mara doesn't know what or who she can trust and how she can keep everyone safe from herself. <br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>I was falling apart and all my pieces were scattering to the wind.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br />How my heart ached for <b>Mara</b>. What do you do when you can't trust those around you. <b>When you can't even trust yourself.</b> When people have told you you're crazy so many times that you, slowly, begin to believe it yourself. Mara is an incredibly unreliable narrator. One where I'm constantly questioning anything she says to me. Yet, I find myself <i>wanting</i> to believe her. Which just leads me to having more and more questions about everything and everyone. <br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote> . . . no one could protect me from myself. <blockquote></blockquote></blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br /><br />Where do things stand with Noah? He's been there for Mara from the beginning. Trying to help her. Trying to protect her. <br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>She isn't the only one changing. Every day she shapes me into something else.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br />Oh, how I wish I could take <b>Noah</b> into my arms and make everything okay. We learn more about him and his past in Evolution and it was heartbreaking. He's much more damaged than we were led to believe. I loved how supportive he was of Mara. How he <i>always</i> believed her. How he doted on her every whim, despite how crazy it seemed at the moment. He was dedicated to helping her, in being strong for her, and it broke my heart to see that <i>he</i> needed someone to be his rock sometimes. <br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“I must be made of nothing to feels so much nothing.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br /><br /><b>Noah and Mara</b> . . . *happy sigh* I ship it so hard. <u>So hard</u>. They are both damaged in their own ways but they make each other better. I don't think Mara or Noah would be able to survive without each other. <br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“I’m too selfish to leave you,” I said. Noah pulled back so I could see his smile. “I’m too selfish to let you.” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br />*is now a pile of mushy feelings on the floor*<br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote> “If I were to live a thousand years, I would belong to you for all of them. If we were to live a thousand years, I would want you mine in each one.” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br /><br /><b>Mara and her family</b> . . . that's a tough relationship to put into words. It's hard to put on a fake smile and pretend everything is okay when those closest to you don't believe you. But how could she (and I) expect them to? You could see how much they were trying to help her, how they only wanted what was best, but wouldn't listen to her. And when they did, it only reinforced their idea that she was mentally ill. Which is completely understandable but still a hard pill to swallow (no pun intended). <br /><br /><b>Everybody else</b> . . . is pretty much crazy. With a few exceptions, like Jamie, who still manages to make me laugh my ass off. Other than that, crazy. The sheer insanity . . . it's just too much to put into words. <br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>Noah acted like he felt nothing because he felt everything. He seemed not to care because he cared too much.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br /><br />Creep factor = very high. You've been warned. Some scenes literally had my heart <i>
  <b>pounding</b>
</i>. And it was achieved by the simplest things. There were a few instances where I felt like things were a little <i>too</i> dramatic in order to get a reaction out of the reader. I didn't think all the writing in blood and dead animals were necessary. They were a little over-the-top for me. Other than that, I was thoroughly creeped out. <br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>My hair was plastered to my face, and I was pale. But I looked okay. Maybe a little thin. A little tired. But normal.<br />Then my reflection winked. Even though I didn't.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br />I don't know how Mara manages . . . I would've been a vegetable by then. <br /><br /><b>The writing</b> was flawless. Michelle Hodkin creates a story with the perfect amount of humor, angst, mystery, and horror. The writing leaves you entranced and on the edge of your seat. The witty dialogue and dry humor between the characters keeps things from getting too intense. She creates such suspense. Each chapter ending is like a little cliffhanger of it's own. <br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Everyone’s a little crazy. The only difference between us and them is that they hide it better.” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i> <br />This isn't my first rodeo. I read the ending of The Unbecoming of Mara Dyer. I had to wait two years for the rest of the books to be published. With that killer cliffhanger lurking in the back of my mind. <br /><i>I'm prepared for anything,</i> I told myself. <br />I was not. anywhere near. prepared. for anything past 75 percent of the book. <br />Holy sh*tsticks. <br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>They rattled my cage to see if I'd bite. When they released me, they'd see that the answer was yes.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i> <br /><br /><br />Final rating: 4.5 stars <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7568651930158196512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_375033311" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/375033311" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/375033311?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442421790" href="/book/show/12950372-the-evolution-of-mara-dyer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer375033311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8428540729204474833">Well wasn't this a pleasant surprise! After being hugely disappointed with the way the first book turned from fabulously creepy to annoyingly romancy, I did not hold very high hopes for its sequel--even though I was (obviously) curious enough by the ending to still be looking forward to it. As you can tell, I had a very up and down relationship with that book. Fortunately, this sequel rocked it way harder than I could have hoped for!<br/><br/>From terrifying hand-made dolls (Dolls. Are. Terrifying!), to d</span>
  <span id="freeText8428540729204474833" style="display:none">Well wasn't this a pleasant surprise! After being hugely disappointed with the way the first book turned from fabulously creepy to annoyingly romancy, I did not hold very high hopes for its sequel--even though I was (obviously) curious enough by the ending to still be looking forward to it. As you can tell, I had a very up and down relationship with that book. Fortunately, this sequel rocked it way harder than I could have hoped for!<br><br>From terrifying hand-made dolls (Dolls. Are. Terrifying!), to dead crows dropping from the sky(!!!), to mental hospitals (the ones with the freaks!), The Evolution of Mara Dyer puts the creep in creepy! &lt;--Win! I mean, someone watching her sleep! That has to give you the heebie-jeebies! (Hear that Mr. Cullen!!?) This part is was I enjoyed the most from the first book and was doubly glad to see again in an even higher degree in this sequel. The pacing was a great match as well with the perfect amount of spine chilling happenings that kept me positively glued to it all. To balance it out, we get some fantastic humor that made me burst into laughter more than once! I especially adore Jamie's sarcasm! Even Noah made me laugh - which is in high contrast to my initial reaction to him. And this time, the romance did not give everything else a back seat. It's still largely present, but, surprisingly, I even enjoyed that part!<br><br>The romance in the first book completely threw me off. I didn't like the love interest; I got annoyed by Noah's perfectness coupled with an arrogant attitude. But worst of all, a deliciously creepy plot was forgotten for this uninviting romance. So colour me surprised when I found myself pleasantly enjoying the romance in this installment. Not only did I not remember why I didn't like Noah at first--which I'm sure helped a ton--it is kept <i>a part of</i> the plot, not squashing it. Plus, Noah's character has clearly grown, he's <i>good</i> to Mara. He grounds her when she's feels she's falling off the brink of insanity; I really liked that about him. I also thought the chemistry between the two was absolutely electric. <br><br>Another disappointment in the first Mara was the whole non-answer to her "power". She just was. It felt so bland after all the scenarios I had been wildly imagining. I shouldn't have come to such quick conclusions, however, as we delve into some very intriguing and super interesting plot development that gives a much more satisfying answer to that part of the story. Although we didn't get all the answers in this one either, but at least I know there is one better than "just because". <br><br>Aside from some blatantly obvious "twists" where I cursed Mara for not having put two and two together sooner, I highly enjoyed this sequel and I'm incredibly happy I gave it a try after my less than enthusiastic response to book 1. For fans of the first, you will love it I assure you, for non-fans of the first, you will more than likely love it too!<br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380346185i/700655.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8428540729204474833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1158283481" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1158283481" />
    <a title="TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34338862-thecrazyworldofabooklover"><img alt="TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489089790p2/34338862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1158283481?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover" href="/user/show/34338862-thecrazyworldofabooklover">TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34338862-thecrazyworldofabooklover?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1158283481" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17413940985521987986"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496681730i/22942271._SY540_.jpg' width='450' height='450' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>A little tally to begin:<br/><br/><b>Number of times I screamed “W.T.F!!???” out loud - 96<br/><br/>Number of times I was actually scared to leave my room because of all the creepy things happening – 8 <br/><br/>Number of times I had to put my kindle down and just stare at the wall to fully digest WTF had just happened – 11<br/><br/>Number of times I wished I was 17 because I was SWOONING HARD OVER NOAH FREAKING SHAW- 3,857,892,357</b><br/><br/>How a book can make me afraid to leave the safety of my bed and needing to turn the lights on to do so in on</span>
  <span id="freeText17413940985521987986" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1496681730i/22942271._SY540_.jpg" width="450" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A little tally to begin:<br><br><b>Number of times I screamed “W.T.F!!???” out loud - 96<br><br>Number of times I was actually scared to leave my room because of all the creepy things happening – 8 <br><br>Number of times I had to put my kindle down and just stare at the wall to fully digest WTF had just happened – 11<br><br>Number of times I wished I was 17 because I was SWOONING HARD OVER NOAH FREAKING SHAW- 3,857,892,357</b><br><br>How a book can make me afraid to leave the safety of my bed and needing to turn the lights on to do so in one chapter then have me drooling over a 17 year old in the next is beyond comprehension. But HOLY SHIT this book did. The first book in this series had me scratching my head, questioning everyone and everything, but this book….<b>THIS BOOK has had my heart pounding, heart swooning, nerves on edge, mind reeling, and my jaw on the floor. And again questioning EVERYTHING.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439912386i/15903263.jpg" width="450" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I obviously cannot go into any detail about what happens in this book because that would just ruin the experience of reading the first. But I can say IT IS BRILLIANT. The webs of the plot just keep getting deeper and more twisted, and that ending?!?! I REFUSE. No. It’s not true. I will not believe it! NOPE!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439912387i/15903264.jpg" width="450" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Michelle’s writing is fantastic. Each scene leapt off the page and made me feel like I was there. And even though this is YA- the romance in it is <b>JUST BEAUTIFUL. Some of the most romantic lines I have EVER read.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439912387i/15903265.jpg" width="450" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>READ IT. Read it read it read it. This may take some people out of their comfort zone because of the genres, but it is most definitely worth the wild ride it takes you on! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439912386i/15903262.jpg" width="450" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*Now excuse me- I am locking myself away to read book 3. With all the lights on. And the blinds shut. With a baseball bat clutched in my hand. <br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/2s9O6ty">http://amzn.to/2s9O6ty</a> <br><br><a href="https://thecrazyworldofabooklover.wordpress.com/" target="blog" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467902722i/19644381._SX540_.jpg" width="275" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> <br>Find Me On:<br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/thecrazyworldofabooklover/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ❤ <a href="https://www.facebook.com/profile.php?id=100009277089211" rel="nofollow noopener">FB Page</a> ❤ <a href="https://www.facebook.com/TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover/" rel="nofollow noopener">FB Blog</a> ❤ <a href="https://thecrazyworldofabooklover.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> ❤ <a href="https://twitter.com/_StephDeMarco_" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></span>
